<div id="review_1214600073" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1214600073" />
    <a title="JenniferD" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2635637-jenniferd"><img alt="JenniferD" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521134725p2/2635637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1214600073?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JenniferD" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JenniferD" href="/user/show/2635637-jenniferd">JenniferD</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2635637-jenniferd?shelf=2015-books">2015-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2635637-jenniferd?shelf=in-translation">in-translation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1214600073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2394611294857434311">2.5- stars, really.<br/><br/>okay, first up: hello, my name is jennifer and i got a bit suckered into reading a romance novel. :/ <br/><br/>(publisher lists this as 'fiction, romance, contemporary' - NetGalley listing reads 'literature/fiction' and did not have the 'contemporary romance' identifier.) i am not against romance, per se, but in reading, i am against the overly-sentimental and schmaltzy, and overuse of clichés. so this book fell apart for me on all three counts. which is really, really unfortunate. this</span>
  <span id="freeText2394611294857434311" style="display:none">2.5- stars, really.<br /><br />okay, first up: hello, my name is jennifer and i got a bit suckered into reading a romance novel. :/ <br /><br />(publisher lists this as 'fiction, romance, contemporary' - NetGalley listing reads 'literature/fiction' and did not have the 'contemporary romance' identifier.) i am not against romance, per se, but in reading, i am against the overly-sentimental and schmaltzy, and overuse of clichés. so this book fell apart for me on all three counts. which is really, really unfortunate. this is a book about books, and their power to help and to heal. it's set in paris, and the bookshop is a floating barge on the seine. i mean... come on! but the books and bookshop are a feint for the love story (actually, a few love stories - the primary of which is pretty thin and, for me, difficult to believe).<br /><br />i probably should have clued in right away that this wasn't going to be the best read for me - the main character's name is 'perdu', french for lost or missing. and perdu - jean perdu - has shut himself off to experiencing the world after the heartbreak of being dumped 21 years ago. (le sigh.) jean perdu is truly, emotionally and physically lost. it's a bit too literal for my tastes. jean was left a letter by his departing girlfriend (again, a literal 'dear john' letter), but he could not bring himself to read it for more than 20 years.<br /><br />the book, at moments, reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18293427.The_Storied_Life_of_A_J__Fikry" title="The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry by Gabrielle Zevin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13227454.The_Unlikely_Pilgrimage_of_Harold_Fry" title="The Unlikely Pilgrimage of Harold Fry by Rachel Joyce" rel="nofollow noopener">The Unlikely Pilgrimage of Harold Fry</a> - both charming, nice novels with interesting premises and some endearing secondary characters. <i>the little paris bookshop</i>, though, is not as strong as these and mostly it's because of the schmaltz and clichés. i felt like i was reading regurgitations and not originality.<br /><br />there was also this very strange situation where jean perdu's father goes on a bit with a long comparison of horses and women. this came right at a moment during the read where i was feeling awkward about how men and women were being presented/treated in the story, and i found myself off on a tangent wondering what the author really felt about men and women. a passing mention of someone being a misogynist happens later in the story. i'm not explaining this very well, sorry. but i felt strange that the author was female, yet offering stereotypical thoughts that might usually come from a (less-than-evolved) male perspective.<br /><br />so as to not sound so old and cranky and down on love (i am none of these things, i swear!): i did really enjoy the meta-ness of the book. as i was reading, i was marking the authors and books mentioned in the story. helpfully, the author and publisher have included a list at the back of the book. as well, there was some good eating happening through the novel. a few recipes are also listed at the back of the book. so both of these aspects were great. the book, originally published in Germany as <i>Das Lavendelzimmer</i> (The Lavender Room) has been a huge hit for george - more than 500,000 copies have bene sold, and its won two awards - DeLiA and the Glauser-Prize.<br /><br />so, clearly this book has worked for, and is beloved by, many readers. i just really wish the whole of the thing was stronger and more engaging for me.<br /><br />(ARC (e-pub edition) provided by the publisher, via NetGalley)<br /><br /><br />edited to add: <br /><br />1. i made a listopia for the books mentioned in <i>the little paris bookshop</i>. it makes for a pretty great reading project. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/85533.Jean_Perdu_s_Emergency_Literary_Pharmacy">https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/8...</a><br /><br />2. authors mentioned, though no specific books noted:<br /><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6410.Alice_Munro" title="Alice Munro" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice Munro</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/235.Thomas_Pynchon" title="Thomas Pynchon" rel="nofollow noopener">Thomas Pynchon</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/101107.Marcel_Pagnol" title="Marcel Pagnol" rel="nofollow noopener">Marcel Pagnol</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/32878.Michel_Houellebecq" title="Michel Houellebecq" rel="nofollow noopener">Michel Houellebecq</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3075.John_Irving" title="John Irving" rel="nofollow noopener">John Irving</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/463.Philip_Roth" title="Philip Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Philip Roth</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/51575.Colette" title="Colette" rel="nofollow noopener">Colette</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1464.George_Sand" title="George Sand" rel="nofollow noopener">George Sand</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3137322.Fyodor_Dostoyevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoyevsky" rel="nofollow noopener">Fyodor Dostoyevsky</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7423689.Hildegard_von_Bingen" title="Hildegard von Bingen" rel="nofollow noopener">Hildegard von Bingen</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1113469.Hermann_Hesse" title="Hermann Hesse" rel="nofollow noopener">Hermann Hesse</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/957894.Albert_Camus" title="Albert Camus" rel="nofollow noopener">Albert Camus</a><br />* <a <div id="review_2912920112" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2912920112" />
    <a title="Tina Haigler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30268418-tina-haigler"><img alt="Tina Haigler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396641790p2/30268418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2912920112?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina Haigler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina Haigler" href="/user/show/30268418-tina-haigler">Tina Haigler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553418798" href="/book/show/28503688-the-little-paris-bookshop">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2912920112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13161710683794575231"><b>
  <i>"How on earth could I have let them talk me into it?"</i>
</b><br/><br/>Holy bejeezus! If this book is any indication, French people really are romantic. At least the woman who wrote this novel is. I would love to think French men think as romantically as this author portrays them, but I highly doubt it. I suspect it is merely wishful thinking on her part, but oh how wonderful it would be to be entirely wrong.<br/><br/>This was a sad, yet beautiful story about love, loss, friendship, and the stages of grief. It's the ta</span>
  <span id="freeText13161710683794575231" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"How on earth could I have let them talk me into it?"</i>
</b><br /><br />Holy bejeezus! If this book is any indication, French people really are romantic. At least the woman who wrote this novel is. I would love to think French men think as romantically as this author portrays them, but I highly doubt it. I suspect it is merely wishful thinking on her part, but oh how wonderful it would be to be entirely wrong.<br /><br />This was a sad, yet beautiful story about love, loss, friendship, and the stages of grief. It's the tale of a man, Jean Perdu, who instead of dealing with the pain of loss, decides to avoid it and ignore it altogether for twenty years, until new circumstances cause the old emotions to surface once again.<br /><br />Reading about the countryside was so relaxing for me. Wonderfully told, it made me feel like I was visiting France, visiting vineyards, and sailing down the Seine myself. On top of that, the romance in the way the main character thought and how he viewed life, was enough to make a hopeless romantic like me quite weak in the knees. Plus he absolutely loves books. I mean what more can a girl ask for? My only complaint is that due to it being translated from French, every now and then you'll come across sentences that don't fully translate the true feeling of the original text.<br /><br />Ultimately, this was very moving and sweet. I highly recommend it to anyone who loves romance, France, journeys, adventures, sailing, vineyards, stories about self-awakening, or books about books. As Perdu would say, this book is best read in a cozy setting, with a nice glass of wine in hand.<br /><br /><b>"(Also known as living.)"</b><br /><br />*I also listened to the audio book. It was done well. The voices chosen for the characters fit their personalities and the narrator did the different accents quite well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13161710683794575231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1373887669?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathrine ☯️ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathrine ☯️ " href="/user/show/22600410-cathrine">Cathrine ☯️ </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22600410-cathrine?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1373887669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14947923643368049223">I just cannot get into this. Is it the structure, the translation, me, what? Based on other poor ratings and general boredom I am giving up. Other books are waiting. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8561724541832551926">I was going to rate this 3 stars but I realized that I skimmed the last third of the book because I just wanted to be done with it. The tone of the book kept changing. Was it a romance with the idea of selling books as much a part of the romance as those between characters? But then our bookseller Perdu takes off on his bookselling boat on a river road trip. He picks up this wierd young writer who wears earmuffs all the time and it becomes a farce.   <span id="freeText8561724541832551926" style="display:none">I was going to rate this 3 stars but I realized that I skimmed the last third of the book because I just wanted to be done with it. The tone of the book kept changing. Was it a romance with the idea of selling books as much a part of the romance as those between characters? But then our bookseller Perdu takes off on his bookselling boat on a river road trip. He picks up this wierd young writer who wears earmuffs all the time and it becomes a farce. They have no money and no food and have to pay fees to tie up the boat at various destinations. But then suddenly they get out and visit an ATM for funds. WTW? The love scenes throughout the book were not very compelling and occasionally the use of terms that fit more in erotica than this book had me wondering was it a problem with the translation or something else. Unexplicably Perdu abandons the boat for a car trip (the map in the front of the book gives this away so this is not a spoiler). Perdu is on a search for a lost love and avoiding any new ones. Anyway I've already invested too much time in reviewing this unsatisfying book, sigh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8561724541832551926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1685939551" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1685939551" />
    <a title="Jacob Overmark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41670556-jacob-overmark"><img alt="Jacob Overmark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595533530p2/41670556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1685939551?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Overmark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Overmark" href="/user/show/41670556-jacob-overmark">Jacob Overmark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780349140377" href="/book/show/28951781-the-little-paris-bookshop">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41670556-jacob-overmark?shelf=contemporary-international">contemporary-international</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41670556-jacob-overmark?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41670556-jacob-overmark?shelf=read-owned">read-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41670556-jacob-overmark?shelf=german-language-authors">german-language-authors</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1685939551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11526700807252689621">What did I think? <br/><br/>At first I thought "What´s not to like?". A book about books and Southern France, perfect for a rainy summer day and I immediately fell for Jean Perdu.<br/><br/>The name game wasn´t lost on me, a man in a mature age, lost in himself, in his past and his happy and unhappy memories. He could have been "The Steppenwolf" or even the narrator in "À la recherche du temps perdu", but he´s neither. <br/><br/>He is a man with a mission, he is a literary apothecary, caring for all the lost souls but his own</span>
  <span id="freeText11526700807252689621" style="display:none">What did I think? <br /><br />At first I thought "What´s not to like?". A book about books and Southern France, perfect for a rainy summer day and I immediately fell for Jean Perdu.<br /><br />The name game wasn´t lost on me, a man in a mature age, lost in himself, in his past and his happy and unhappy memories. He could have been "The Steppenwolf" or even the narrator in "À la recherche du temps perdu", but he´s neither. <br /><br />He is a man with a mission, he is a literary apothecary, caring for all the lost souls but his own with the remedy he knows best, books. <br /><br />While a few love stories slowly unfold, at a pace set to make you think and contemplate, you are invited to take a walk down your own memory lane.<br /><br />Which books were part of your life in which circumstances. Which books made you cry because they touched some deep memory, which books were like your reflection in dark waters or which books inspired you to live, love and do great things. <br /><br />Some do yoga, some read, some buy a sports car, we all handle our lives in different ways. "The Little Paris Bookshop" does not pretend to give you a recipe for a long happy life. <br />It merely points out that whatever you are, you are a product of your life and your experiences, some sad and some happy and people able to include their past in the present stands good chances of many happy moments.<br /><br />To me a 5-star reading experience is one that make me reflect on life, my own and in general. Even "The Little Paris Bookshop" can hardly be considered Nobel material, it did the trick for me.<br /><br />Happy reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11526700807252689621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1156979896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156979896" />
    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5246491-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400547572p2/5246491.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156979896?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/5246491-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780553418781" href="/book/show/23278273-the-little-paris-bookshop">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156979896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7058563358177407073">You fall in love with this book first because it's about the power of books. Who can resist the idea of a book barge on the Seine in Paris where the bookseller, Jean Perdu, uses his intuition to select just the right book to deal with whichever emotion - small or large - is afflicting you? Monsieur Perdu explains it as <i>"I wanted to treat feelings that are not recognized as afflictions and are never diagnosed by doctors. All those little feelings and emotions no therapist is interested in, becaus</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7058563358177407073" style="display:none">You fall in love with this book first because it's about the power of books. Who can resist the idea of a book barge on the Seine in Paris where the bookseller, Jean Perdu, uses his intuition to select just the right book to deal with whichever emotion - small or large - is afflicting you? Monsieur Perdu explains it as <i>"I wanted to treat feelings that are not recognized as afflictions and are never diagnosed by doctors. All those little feelings and emotions no therapist is interested in, because they are apparently too minor and intangible. The feeling that washes over you when another summer nears its end Or when you recognize that you haven't got your whole life left to find out where you belong. Or the slight sense of grief when a friendship doesn't develop as you thought, and you have to continue your search for a lifelong companion. Or those birthday morning blues. Nostalgia for the air of your childhood. Things like that."</i> <br /><br />After a while, you'll move to a deeper appreciation as you realize the book is about grief. And life. And facing death. On her website (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nina-george.com">http://www.nina-george.com</a>), Nina George says:<br /><br /><i>It took me 20 years to become famous overnight—from 1993 to 2013, when The Little Paris Bookshop landed on the bestseller list. [Note: German bestseller list].This long journey was necessary. I had to live, write a great deal, love and weep. I had to lose everything before I could write what I was capable of, what really interested me. Everyone must follow their own journey. Usually a painful one. <br /><br />The Little Paris Bookshop was the result of a breakthrough. I’d always known I wanted to write about death, about the fear of death and how this fear holds us back from living life to the fullest.</i> <br /><br />In the book, we go on the journey of Perdu as he moves from being lost in grief to slowly reclaiming himself and his life. The further south we go, the warmer the weather and the more Perdu comes alive. Bookseller. Lost love. The wisdom of books. It likely sounds rather similar to The Storied Life of A.J. Fikry, which in some ways it is. I preferred The Little Paris Bookshop, likely because it was quirkier and more whimsical. The story would so easily translate into a subtitled French movie along the lines of "Amelie."<br /><br />As someone with a degree in French, I loved just how truly French it all felt. At first, it was surprising how well this was done as Nina George is German, but it turns out she lives in both Germany and France. Her intimacy with France pays off. Thanks to the gorgeous descriptions, I wouldn't be surprised to see an uptick in Americans heading to Provence after reading The Little Paris Bookshop! <br /><br />George's writing is wonderful (and kudos should go to the translator for the fantastic work on this English edition). I ended up sharing several quotes to Goodreads - way more than I have for any book in a long while. George beautifully captures so many emotions and ideas.<br /><br />But back to the books and which ones best fit different emotions. At the end of the book, there's "Jean Perdu's Emergency Literary Pharmacy" and among the "fast-acting medicines for minds and hearts affected by minor or moderate emotional turmoil," you'll find:<br /><br /><b>Adams, Douglas.</b> <i>The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy: A Trilogy in Five Parts</i><br />Effective in large doses for treating pathological optimism or a sense of humor failure. Ideal for saunagoers with exhibitionist tendencies. <br />Side effects: An aversion to owning things, and a potentially chronic tendency to wear a robe all day.<br /><br />Thanks to Crown and Netgalley for providing an advance copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7058563358177407073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1161857564" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1161857564" />
    <a title="Erin " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2997696-erin"><img alt="Erin " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531863934p2/2997696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1161857564?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin " href="/user/show/2997696-erin">Erin </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1161857564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10142810638993230328">Historic fiction is my preferred stomping ground, but I’ve a reputation for venturing into multiple genres. I think journeying outside my comfort zone challenges me and helps me retain perspective as a reviewer which is how I found myself staring down a copy of Nina George’s contemporary romance, The Little Paris Bookshop. <br/><br/>Looking back, I can honestly say the story made almost no impression on me. I didn’t connect with any of the characters and I couldn’t rouse much enthusiasm for their personal</span>
  <span id="freeText10142810638993230328" style="display:none">Historic fiction is my preferred stomping ground, but I’ve a reputation for venturing into multiple genres. I think journeying outside my comfort zone challenges me and helps me retain perspective as a reviewer which is how I found myself staring down a copy of Nina George’s contemporary romance, The Little Paris Bookshop. <br /><br />Looking back, I can honestly say the story made almost no impression on me. I didn’t connect with any of the characters and I couldn’t rouse much enthusiasm for their personal trials. Jean, Manon, I couldn’t care less if you paid me. I found the romantic elements overly sentimental and was easily bored with the direction of the narrative. I tried my best, but it just didn’t take. <br /><br />That said, I don’t consider the experience a total wash. I loved the idea of the literary apothecary and can’t deny falling for George’s prose. My notebook is covered with lines from the book, sentences that spoke directly to my love of literature. I wasn’t buying the story George was peddling, but I liked her point of view and how she captured the heart and soul of the literary community in plain black and white text.<br /><br />At the end of the day, The Little Paris Bookshop wasn’t my cuppa tea. I wouldn’t recommend it, but I enjoyed the language and style in which the written. The setting was decent, but the plot plodding. Interesting from a literary perspective, but not the engaging tale I’d hoped for going in. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10142810638993230328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Connie G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Connie G" href="/user/show/5364077-connie-g">Connie G</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1551841096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11726074110901682970">I love books about bookstores so I was excited to start "The Little Paris Bookshop". Monsieur Jean Perdu's literary apothecary is located on a barge moored on the Seine. Perdu senses people's needs and problems, and prescribes books that are perfect for each customer. Unfortunately, he has been unable to deal with his own heartache since the love of his life left him 21 years ago. His lover had left him a letter when she departed from Paris, but he waited 21 years to finally open it and feels sh</span>
  <span id="freeText11726074110901682970" style="display:none">I love books about bookstores so I was excited to start "The Little Paris Bookshop". Monsieur Jean Perdu's literary apothecary is located on a barge moored on the Seine. Perdu senses people's needs and problems, and prescribes books that are perfect for each customer. Unfortunately, he has been unable to deal with his own heartache since the love of his life left him 21 years ago. His lover had left him a letter when she departed from Paris, but he waited 21 years to finally open it and feels shocked when her reason for leaving him is revealed.<br /><br />Perdu, whose last name is French for "lost", is feeling adrift emotionally. The bookseller embarks on a healing journey to rediscover the wonderful things in life, using all his senses and letting go of his inhibitions. Perdu and Max Jordan, a young popular novelist suffering from writer's block, travel on the book barge through a series of canals to Provence. Their journey exposes them to all the sensory delights of life--the beautiful French countryside, wonderful food and wine, interesting people, and words of wisdom.<br /><br />Their trip sounds like a magical journey that most of us would love. Unfortunately, the writing (or the translation) is so syrupy sweet that it starts to cloy after hundreds of pages. I started thinking about speakers I've heard at poetry lectures, art museums, and concerts--people in touch with their feelings--but couldn't come up with any guy so sugary in their speech. I felt that the author had a great idea for the book, and there were parts I enjoyed, but it was just overdone. 3 1/2 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11726074110901682970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1317466534?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachelle" href="/user/show/2166094-rachelle">Rachelle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1317466534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14021672023941504545">This book was not what I hoped it would be. I really loved the idea of the floating book apothecary, and think so much more could have been done with that idea. In the end, though, this book was rather a disappointment. First, I didn't really love any of the characters, especially Manon, the woman Jean is so tortured with love for all these years. Why? She was selfish and didn't have any clue what commitment meant. Jean just came across as a fool who somewhere along the way mistook lust for love</span>
  <span id="freeText14021672023941504545" style="display:none">This book was not what I hoped it would be. I really loved the idea of the floating book apothecary, and think so much more could have been done with that idea. In the end, though, this book was rather a disappointment. First, I didn't really love any of the characters, especially Manon, the woman Jean is so tortured with love for all these years. Why? She was selfish and didn't have any clue what commitment meant. Jean just came across as a fool who somewhere along the way mistook lust for love, and ruined his whole life over it. In fact, there was just way too much lust and not a whole lot of real love in this whole book. I had to skip a few too many pages. The flow wasn't great -it was all over the place, and some parts of Jean wallowing just got to be too much. And though much of the language and descriptions were quite poetic and lovely, it seemed like the narrator, Jean, Manon, and even Manon's mother all had the same voice: the author obviously loves beautiful language, but it didn't seem real to me that everyone would write that way. You can change the font, but it still sounds like it is coming from the same person. Hey, but at least I finished it, so that is saying something. I have to learn that just because a book has "Paris" and "books" in the title does not mean it is worth my time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14021672023941504545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1227682192" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1227682192" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1227682192?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25393301-the-little-paris-bookshop">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=society">society</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1227682192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14917221875809814833"><br/><i>"A book is both medic and medicine at once. It makes a diagnosis as well as offering therpay. Putting the right novels to the appropriate ailments:that's how I sell books"</i><br/><br/>Fifty year old John Perdu considers himself a dispenser of literary medicine for ailments of the human soul rather than a mere bookseller. From his barge, the Literary Apothecary, moored on the Seine in Paris he dispenses books to cure people of their ailments, whether it be sadness, disappointment, anxiety or a lost love.<br/><br/><i>"When</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14917221875809814833" style="display:none"><br /><i>"A book is both medic and medicine at once. It makes a diagnosis as well as offering therpay. Putting the right novels to the appropriate ailments:that's how I sell books"</i><br /><br />Fifty year old John Perdu considers himself a dispenser of literary medicine for ailments of the human soul rather than a mere bookseller. From his barge, the Literary Apothecary, moored on the Seine in Paris he dispenses books to cure people of their ailments, whether it be sadness, disappointment, anxiety or a lost love.<br /><br /><i>"Whenever Monsieur Perdu looked at a book, he did not see it purely in terms of a story, retail price and an essential balm for the soul; he saw freedom on wings of paper"</i> <br /><br /><i>"Perdu reflected that is was a common misconception that booksellers looked after books. They look after people."</i><br /><br />Perdu has a book for every occasion and every need. However,the only person he has failed to cure is himself. Since the love of his life, Manon, left him twenty one years ago to return to her husband in the south of France, he has led a lonely and insular life and has never been able to move on. He prescribes books for his landlady and the tenants of his apartment building, who try to befriend him but he remains distant.<br /><br /><i>"Habit is a vain and treachorous goddess. She lets nothing disrupt her rule. She smothers one desire after another: the desire to travel, the desire for a better job or a new love. She stops us from living as we would like, because, habit prevents us from asking ourselves whether we continue to enjoy doing what we do."</i> <br /><br />Until one day a new tenant moves in, Catherine who has been left by her husband and is alone and sad. When Perdu gives her an old table and chair to help furnish her apartment, she finds an unopened letter from Manon sent to Perdu not long after she left him. Finally reading it, he realises he has been wrong in the assumptions he has made and based his life on and he is suddenly galvanised into action and the adventure of a lifetime. Along with him for the ride is his young friend Max Jordan, a writer suffering from writer's block after his debut book became a run away best seller.<br /><br />Nina George's characters are well crafted and develop into real people as the story progresses. Her writing is wonderfully evocative, Perdu's wisdom in intuitively knowing what people need serves him well and never more so than when he starts to live his life again. Under his wing, young Max also realises the possibilities the world has to offer. There is love and friendship and sensuality. Cuneo, the Italian who joins them later in the novel cooks them wonderful food and the smells and flavours leap from the book.<br /><br /><i>"With every bite of food steeped in the herbs and oils of Provence he seemed to absorb a little more of the land that lay ahead; it was as if he were eating the surrounding countryside."</i> <br /><br />This is a wonderful story of lost love and missed opportunities with the message that it's never too late for redemption and new love. There is a lot of wry humour along the way and a few unexpected twists which go together to make a very satisfying read. <br /><br />One final quote on the power of books:<br /><br /><i>"Books are more than doctors, of course. Some novels are loving, lifelong companions;some give you a clip around the ear; others are friends who wrap you in warm towels when you've got those autumn blues. And some...well, some are pink candy floss that tingles in your brain for three seconds and leaves a blissful voice. Like a short, torrid love affair."</i><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14917221875809814833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1737978353" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1737978353" />
    <a title="Suzy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6942006-suzy"><img alt="Suzy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565275031p2/6942006.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1737978353?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzy" href="/user/show/6942006-suzy">Suzy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942006-suzy?shelf=found-community">found-community</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942006-suzy?shelf=journeying">journeying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942006-suzy?shelf=found-family">found-family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6942006-suzy?shelf=books-n-bookshops">books-n-bookshops</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1737978353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6223547743396721492">This story of a Parisian bookseller who sets out on his bookstore on a barge to find the lover who abandoned him 20 years ago started out on a promising note but very quickly devolved. So many times I was rolling my eyes and groaning . . . and not in a good way. :) I felt the author was trying way too hard to be poignant and profound - maybe wanting to be the next Elizabeth Gilbert?<br/><br/>So why did I read to the end of this almost 400 page book and rate it 3 stars instead of 1 or 2? There were several</span>
  <span id="freeText6223547743396721492" style="display:none">This story of a Parisian bookseller who sets out on his bookstore on a barge to find the lover who abandoned him 20 years ago started out on a promising note but very quickly devolved. So many times I was rolling my eyes and groaning . . . and not in a good way. :) I felt the author was trying way too hard to be poignant and profound - maybe wanting to be the next Elizabeth Gilbert?<br /><br />So why did I read to the end of this almost 400 page book and rate it 3 stars instead of 1 or 2? There were several things I did enjoy, primarily the descriptions of place. The book starts in Paris and our bookseller, Jean Perdu, travels partially by boat and then by car to Sanary-sur-Mer on the Mediterranean. I felt like I was taking the journey with them, experiencing the country through their eyes. I also loved the idea that Perdu's bookstore on a boat was billed as a Literary Apothecary, where instead of just selling books, he would prescribe books based on what customers needed. He was writing an encyclopedia of "small emotions" as a guide to selecting books for specific things people were feeling. Clever! Lastly, I came to like many of the characters and they are (amazingly) sticking with me.<br /><br />But there were not enough of those good things for me to endorse this book. And what about the title? I didn't get the feeling that this bookshop was little and 2/3 of the book does not take place in Paris - since the bookstore was on a boat, he took it with him. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6223547743396721492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1179365089" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1179365089" />
    <a title="Olga Godim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim"><img alt="Olga Godim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442639299p2/7438487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1179365089?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olga Godim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olga Godim" href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim">Olga Godim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7438487-olga-godim?shelf=mainstream">mainstream</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1179365089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2516540570836140949"><i>I received this Kindle uncorrected proof from NetGalley.</i><br/><br/>A wonderful book, one of the best I’ve read recently. It’s full of marvelous quotes, despite being a translation. Isn’t it interesting? The book was originally written in German. It takes place in France, with most of the characters French. And I’ve read it in English.<br/>Human life in all its absurdity and beauty, warmth and ugliness stands up from the pages of this novel. Grief and betrayal, cowardice and pride, kindness and compassion, men a</span>
  <span id="freeText2516540570836140949" style="display:none"><i>I received this Kindle uncorrected proof from NetGalley.</i><br /><br />A wonderful book, one of the best I’ve read recently. It’s full of marvelous quotes, despite being a translation. Isn’t it interesting? The book was originally written in German. It takes place in France, with most of the characters French. And I’ve read it in English.<br />Human life in all its absurdity and beauty, warmth and ugliness stands up from the pages of this novel. Grief and betrayal, cowardice and pride, kindness and compassion, men and women – they are all there, in that file on my Kindle. And of course, there are books. The protagonist, Jean Perdu, is a bookseller. He loves books. He sells books. And he treats his books as medicine for the soul. His floating bookstore on a barge is even called Literary Apothecary. <br /><blockquote>“… a book is both medic and medicine at once. It makes a diagnosis as well as offering therapy. Putting the right novels to the appropriate ailments: that’s how I sell books.”<br />~~~~~~~~~~~<br />Perdu reflected that it is a common misconception that booksellers looked after books. They look after people.<br />~~~~~~~~~~~<br />He wanted her to sense the boundless possibilities offered by books. There would always be enough. They would never stop loving their readers. <br />~~~~~~~~~~~ </blockquote> It’s fitting that a story about a bookseller has multiple literary allusions. To start with, it takes place on boat. Three men and [no, not a dog] two cats travel on this boat down the waterways of France from Paris to Provence. Each one is on a personal quest: to find love, to reach absolution, to gain experience, to escape the past. Each one is searching for his story. <br />Jean Perdu’s story starts and ends with a woman. Two different women bookend his tale, but the story is not about them. It’s about Jean’s emotional journey, his belated maturing, his grief and his growth. The memories of his first love haunt him, driving him to analyze his former decisions, to atone for his betrayal, if he ever hopes to be worthy of his new love. <br />Despite the touchy topic, the author wouldn’t allow sentimentality to spoil her book. The supporting characters all act as counterpoints for Jean’s deep digging into his soul. When he gets too lachrymose, forcing my own tears to the surface, another character would come along, say something ridiculous, or snarky, or totally irrelevant, and the spell would be broken, making me chuckle with delight. Throughout the novel, emotions throb, but humor finds a way to balance the scores. From the edge of tears to laughter is a very short step, but the author needs courage to take that step. Nina George doesn’t lack courage. <br />While her hero Jean is mending his broken heart, his everyday life goes on. He sells books. He chats with people. He gets hungry and dreams of a good detergent to get his shirt clean. His boat trip reflects reality to a degree, but on the other hand, it doesn’t resemble reality at all. <br />Nobody I know, nobody sane in any case, mourns for his lost love for 20 years or denies himself any pleasure of the body for that long. Maybe such people exist somewhere but not in my neighborhood. So this is not a story about a guy next door. It’s a story that morphs into a fable, almost a fairy tale. The story in its entirety reads like a metaphor of living and loving and the inescapable link between the two. One doesn’t exist without the other, and for most men, the trigger and the reason for both is a woman. At least it is so from Jean’s point of view. <br />His contemplations are often profound and cover many sad topics—aging and fear, inertia and death. I wish I encountered him when I was younger. If I did, maybe I wouldn’t have made so many mistakes in my life. Or maybe I wasn’t ready for his revelations then. He wasn’t as wise when he was young either. He made his own mistakes aplenty. If he didn’t, this book wouldn’t have been written. <blockquote><i>Oh, dammit. Nobody would ever wise up if they hadn’t at some stage been young and stupid.</i> <br />~~~~~~~~~~~<br />“Fear transforms your body like an inept sculptor does a perfect block of stone,” Perdu heard Vijaya’s voice say inside him. “It’s just that you’re chipped away at from within, and no one sees how many splinters and layers have been taken off you. You become ever thinner and more brittle inside, until even the slightest emotion bowls you over. One hug, and you think you’re going to shatter and be lost.”<br />If Jordan ever needed a piece of fatherly advice, Perdu would tell him: “Never listen to fear! Fear makes you stupid.”<br />~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><i>Habit is a vain and treacherous goddess. She lets nothing disrupt her rule. She smothers one desire after another: the desire to travel, the desire for a better job or a new love. She stops us from living as we would like, because habit prevents us from asking ourselves whether we continue to enjoy doing what we do. </i><br />~~~~~~~~~~~<br />“You know all about death, huh?” She gave a sad smile. “It—the cancer—is called Lupo. That’s the name Elaia gave it when she was nine. Lupo, like the cartoon dog. She imagined that they lived together in her body like housemates. She respects the fact that it sometimes demands more attention. That way, she says, she can rest easier than if she imagines it wants to destroy her. What on earth would destroy its own home?”<br />Zelda smiled lovingly as she gazed at her daughter. “Lupo’s been living with us for more than twenty years. I get the impression that he is starting to feel old and tired too.” <br />~~~~~~~~~~~ </blockquote> A wise and moving novel. Recommended to anyone.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> <br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2516540570836140949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1525895821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1525895821" />
    <a title="Ivana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51836895-ivana"><img alt="Ivana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592400101p2/51836895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1525895821?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivana" href="/user/show/51836895-ivana">Ivana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781410481702" href="/book/show/26199975-the-little-paris-bookshop">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51836895-ivana?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51836895-ivana?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51836895-ivana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1525895821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17684752013784474154">Ah, merde!<br/><br/>I did not read this book. I felt it. I felt every bit of it. It made me experience every word I read in a way that left me breathless. <br/><br/>At first I was amazed by the cuteness and sweetness of the book. It seemed so simple, but not shallow. As I read more I became more and more involved with the characters and their unique stories and personalities. It was so overwhelming feeling so much - I had tears in my eyes for almost half of the book. I felt like crying when something sad happened, </span>
  <span id="freeText17684752013784474154" style="display:none">Ah, merde!<br /><br />I did not read this book. I felt it. I felt every bit of it. It made me experience every word I read in a way that left me breathless. <br /><br />At first I was amazed by the cuteness and sweetness of the book. It seemed so simple, but not shallow. As I read more I became more and more involved with the characters and their unique stories and personalities. It was so overwhelming feeling so much - I had tears in my eyes for almost half of the book. I felt like crying when something sad happened, but also when something happy or nice happened. I couldn't control myself.<br /><br />This book opened so many doors to my soul. I have never before felt so exposed, so fragile, so delicate... and yet, a part of me loves it. I love how much this book touched and caressed my soul. <br /><br />I feel as if it wasn't just that I loved this book, it loved me back. It healed me, maybe all of me, maybe just a bit - It healed me, just like Jean Perdu said: <br /><i>
  <b>"There are books that are suitable for a million people, others for only a hundred. There are even remedies—I mean books—that were written for one person only… A book is both medic and medicine at once. It makes a diagnosis as well as offering therapy."<b><i><br /><br />Perhaps this book was written just for one reader - me. Perhaps it wasn't.<br />In any case, I no longer doubt the healing properties of books!<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bookprejudice.wordpress.com/2016/01/30/the-little-paris-bookshop-review/">https://bookprejudice.wordpress.com/2...</a></i></b></b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17684752013784474154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+sNFuxYzrc/tYINrZdd4juLdHxRzcYAXeR7UlH+mgGQECVhWhDwc9mv9gwNZiTBoVydRWJ1glxHPhSETA4Y5gA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qpNxBxlWQpzL1L8o+CxIdlvAPHDP+V3MEx40nqtbs4ZUWWzqi1nzpU1Jv0DEcgCQ7jpyPCHoSsqlhcEZ13sKYg==')})
  }

J. Fikry\'s life is not at all what he expected it to be. His wife has died; his bookstore is experiencing the worst sales in its history; and now his prized possession, a rare collection of Poe poems, has been stolen. Slowly but surely, he is isolating himself from all the people of Alice Island—from Chief Lambiase, the well-intentioned police officer who\'s always felt kindly toward him; from Ismay, his sister-in-law, who is hell-bent on saving A.J. from his dreary self; from Amelia, the lovely and idealistic (if eccentric) Knightley Press sales rep who persists in taking the ferry to Alice Island, refusing to be deterred by A.J.\'s bad attitude. Even the books in his store have stopped holding pleasure for him. These days, he can only see them as a sign of a world that is changing too rapidly.\n\nAnd then a mysterious package appears at the bookstore. It\'s a small package, though large in weight—an unexpected arrival that gives A.J. the opportunity to make his life over, the ability to see everything anew. It doesn\'t take long for the locals to notice the change overcoming A.J., for the determined sales rep Amelia to see her curmudgeonly client in a new light, for the wisdom of all those books to become again the lifeblood of A.J.\'s world.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/695300.Nina_George">About Nina George</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/695300.Nina_George"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1360524116p3/695300.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/695300.Nina_George">Nina George
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,718
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4940285559875608466">ENG (for German Bio please scroll down).<br/><br/>Born 1973 in Bielefeld, Germany, Nina George is a prize-winning and bestselling author (“Das Lavendelzimmer” – “The Little Paris Bookshop”) and freelance journalist since 1992, who has published 26 books (novels, mysteries and non-fiction) as well as over hundred short stories and more than 600 columns. George has worked as a cop reporter, columnist and mana</span>
  <span id="freeText4940285559875608466" style="display:none">ENG (for German Bio please scroll down).<br /><br />Born 1973 in Bielefeld, Germany, Nina George is a prize-winning and bestselling author (“Das Lavendelzimmer” – “The Little Paris Bookshop”) and freelance journalist since 1992, who has published 26 books (novels, mysteries and non-fiction) as well as over hundred short stories and more than 600 columns. George has worked as a cop reporter, columnist and managing editor for a wide range of publications, including Hamburger Abendblatt, Die Welt, Der Hamburger, “politik und kultur” as well as TV Movie and Federwelt. Georges writes also under three pen-names, for ex “Jean Bagnol”, a double-andronym for provence-based mystery novels. <br /><br />In 2012 and 2013 she won the DeLiA and the Glauser-Prize. In 2013 she had her first bestselling book “Das Lavendelzimmer”, translated in 27 langues and sold more than 500.000 copies. <br /><br />In November 2011, Nina George established the “JA zum Urheberrecht” (YES on Author’s Rights) initiative, which supports the rights of authors, artists and entertainers and is dedicated to resolving issues within the literary community as well as establishing fair and practical rights-license models for the web-distribution. 14 writers’ associations and 27 publishing partners have since joined the JA…-Initiative. George supports the “Initiative Urheberrecht” (Author’s Rights Initiative—<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.urheber.info">www.urheber.info</a>) as well as the “gib 8 aufs Wort”-campaign of the VG Wort. <br /><br />In August 2014 George initiated the Amazon-protest in Germany <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fairer-buchmarkt.de">www.fairer-buchmarkt.de</a>, where overs 2000 germanspeaking authors – Nobelprizewinnig Elfriede Jelinek or Bestsellingauthor Nele Neuhaus – sign an open letter to Jeff Bezos and Amazon, protesting against the banned-book-methods of the giant retailer in the Hachette/Bonnier-dispute. <br /><br />In 2015 George is the founder of the Initiative Fairer Buchmarkt e.V., which supports questions of law in daily business of authors – for ex in contracts, fees or author’s rights and e-Business. <br /><br />George is Member to PEN, Das Syndikat (association of German-language crime writers), the Association of German Authors (VS), the Hamburg Authors’ Association (HAV), BücherFrauen (Women in Publishing), the IACW/AIEP (International Association of Crime Writers), the GEDOK (Association of female artists in Germany), PRO QUOTE and Lean In. Nina George sits on the board of the Three Seas Writers’ and Translaters’ Council (TSWTC), whose members come from 16 different countries. <br /><br />Nina George teaches writing at Literaturbüro Unna, Alsterdamm Kunstschule, Wilhelmsburger Honigfabrik, where she coaches young people, adults and professional authors. <br />George also moderates (bilingual) readings and works as a speaker.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nina-george.com">www.nina-george.com</a><br /><br />find me also on Facebook:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/NinaGeorge.Schriftstellerin?ref=hl">https://www.facebook.com/NinaGeorge.S...</a><br /><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ninageorge.de">www.ninageorge.de</a><br /><br />DE<br /><br />Die mehrfach ausgezeichnete Publizistin Nina George, geboren 1973, veröffentlichte bisher 23 Romane, Krimis, Science-Thriller sowie ca. 88 Kurzgeschichten und über 500 Kolumnen. <br /><br />Ihr Pseudonym Anne West gehört zu den erfolgreichsten deutschsprachigen Erotika-Autorinnen. <br />Für ihren Roman Die Mondspielerin wurde George mit der DeLiA 2011, dem Literaturpreis für den besten Liebesroman des Jahres, ausgezeichnet. Mit dem Wendekrimi Das Licht von Dahme war George 2010 für den Friedrich-Glauser-Preis nominiert. Sie gewann ihn 2012 mit dem in Nigeria angesiedeltem Fußballkrimi „Das Spiel ihres Lebens“. <br /><br />George gründete 2011 die Initiative „JA zum Urheberrecht“, mit der sie sich aktiv für die Rechte aller Kreativarbeiter und Kulturschaffenden gegen die Mentalität der Gratiskultur im Internet einsetzt. <br /><br />Sie ist Mitglied im Syndikat, den Mörderischen Schwestern sowie des Verbands deutscher Schriftsteller.<br />Nina George lebt im Hamburger Grindelviertel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4940285559875608466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
